The Three Meanings of Species
Author defines three meanings of 'naw'' and discusses hierarchy of genera and species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three meanings of 'species' (naw') as used in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Species has three distinct meanings; confusing them leads to category errors in definition.

In Islamic logic, the term 'naw'' (species) is not univocal. This passage clarifies three distinct senses: true species (e.g., a universal predicate of individuals differing in species), species that is not a genus (the species of species, which has no species above it), and species in a general sense. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correct classification and definition, especially in Kalam and Usul al-Fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three meanings
The author lists three: (a) true species (al-naw' al-haqiqi), (b) species not a genus (naw' laysa bi-jins, i.e., species of species), (c) species in the mentioned sense (al-naw' bi al-ma'na al-madhkur, i.e., absolute species).
These meanings are concomitant but conceptually distinct.
2
Examine the two relations of a species to its subordinates
The passage states that a species relates to its subordinates in two ways: first as a predicate (mahmul) and second because the subordinates are not species themselves. The first gives true species-hood; the second makes it the species of species.
3
Differentiate hadd and rasm
If the term 'species' is assigned to only one of these meanings, then a definition (hadd) applies to that one, while for the other a description (rasm)—a necessary mark—suffices.
A definition captures essence; a description only gives a distinguishing property.
4
Recognize homonymy
If 'species' is used for all three meanings, it is a case of verbal homonymy (ishtirak lafzi), meaning the same word has different definitions in each usage.
This avoids equivocation in logical arguments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تحته فهو أنه نوع ليس بجنس، وقياسه إلى ما تحته على وجهين: أحدهما من حيث أنه محمول، وثانيهما من حيث أنها ليست بأنواع؛ فالأول منهما يفيد معنى النوعية الحقيقية، والثاني أنه نوع ليس بجنس فهو نوع الأنواع، ونوع ليس بجنس ونوع بالمعنى المذكور ومفهومات هذه الدلالة وإن كانت متلازمة فهي مفهومات مختلفة. فإذا جعل اسم النوع اسمًا لواحد واحد يكون النوع مقولاً على هذه الثلاثة بالاشتراك اللفظي. وإن جعل اسما لواحد منها فقط كان ذلك القول الذي لذلك الواحد حدًّا له، والقول الذي للآخر رسمًا ليس مفهوم الاسم بل علامة لازمة له. وكما أن تحت نوع الأنواع موضوعات كلية ليست بأنواع نحو العربي والعجمي، فكذلك فوق جنس الأجناس محمولات ليست بأجناس بل معاني لازمة كالوجود دون العرضية. وأما القسمة التي مرَّ ذكرها في الجوهر والجسم وغيرهما إلى الإنسان ففيها نظر؛ إذ الجسم والنفس لم يتناول الملك. وكذلك الناطق، والناطق الذي هو الفصل مقوم للإنسان لا يمكن أن يكون مقولاً على الملك أصلًا يعرف بالتأمل إن شاء الله تعالى.
Under it, it is a species that is not a genus, and its relation to what is under it is in two ways: one from the aspect that it is a predicate, and the second from the aspect that they (the things under it) are not species; so the first of them gives the meaning of true species-hood, and the second is that it is a species not a genus, so it is the species of species, and a species not a genus, and a species in the mentioned sense. And the concepts of these significations, though they are concomitant, are different concepts. So if the name 'species' is made a name for each single one, then 'species' is predicated of these three by verbal homonymy. And if it is made a name for only one of them, then that statement which is for that one is a definition of it, and the statement for the other is a description, not the concept of the name, but a necessary mark for it. And just as under the species of species there are universal subjects that are not species, like Arab and non-Arab, so also above the genus of genera there are predicates that are not genera, but necessary meanings, like existence without accidentality. As for the division that was mentioned concerning substance, body, etc., to man, there is consideration in it; for body and soul do not include angel. Likewise, the rational, and the rational which is the differentia constituting man cannot be predicated of angel at all; this is known by reflection, God willing.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage defines the different meanings of 'species' (naw') and clarifies the hierarchy of genera and species. The author begins by stating that a species which is not a genus relates to its subordinates in two ways: first, as a predicate (i.e., it is predicated of them), and second, because those subordinates are not themselves species. The first provides true species-hood, the second indicates it is a species not a genus, which is the 'species of species' (naw' al-anwa'). The author notes that these three meanings—true species, species not a genus, and species in the mentioned sense—are concomitant but conceptually distinct. If the term 'species' is applied to each, it is homonymous (shared name with different definitions). If applied to only one, then a definition (hadd) applies to that one, while for the other, a description (rasm) (a necessary mark) suffices. The passage then draws an analogy: just as below the species of species there are universal subjects (e.g., Arab, non-Arab) that are not species, so above the genus of genera (jins al-ajnas) there are predicates that are not genera but necessary attributes (e.g., existence). The author critiques a previous division (of substance, body, etc.) as not applying to angel and notes that 'rational' (natiq) as a differentia of man cannot be predicated of angel. This guards against conflating the hierarchical levels and misapplying definitions across categories.

نوع الأنواع
جنس الأجناس
حد

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relation of a species that is not a genus to its subordinates?
A) It is predicated of them and they are species under it.
B) It is predicated of them and they are not species under it.
C) It is not predicated of them but they are species.
D) It is a genus for them.

Key Takeaway
The term 'species' has multiple meanings; failure to differentiate them leads to homonymous definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the term 'jism' (body) and determine which of the three meanings of 'naw'' it could be in a hierarchy of substances. Write a sentence explaining your reasoning.
?
Write a brief note explaining why the term 'species' in 'man is a species' and in 'species of species' are conceptually different, using the hadd/rasm distinction.

Hierarchy of Genera and a Common Error
Author defines three meanings of 'naw'' and discusses hierarchy of genera and species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hierarchy of genera and species and identify an error in assuming a differentia applies across levels.

Core Idea
The hierarchy has limits: a differentia of a lower species may not apply to higher beings.

Building on the meanings of species, this passage discusses the full hierarchy from the highest genus (jins al-ajnas) to the lowest species (species of species) and beyond. It warns against mistakenly extending the differentia of man (rationality) to angels, showing that logical divisions must respect actual categories—a critical insight for Kalam discussions on the nature of angels and other beings.

Guided Path
1
Outline the hierarchy
Identify the highest genus (jins al-ajnas), intermediate genera, and the lowest species (species of species, e.g., 'human'). Under this species are non-species universals like 'Arab' and 'non-Arab'.
The hierarchy is not infinite; it has a top and a bottom.
2
Recognize what is above the highest genus
Above jins al-ajnas there are predicates that are not genera, such as existence (wujud) and other necessary attributes. These are not genera because they are not predicated of things differing in species.
Existence applies to all things but is not a genus; it is a transcendental.
3
Analyze the critique of the division
The author criticizes a previous division (substance, body, etc., to man) for failing to include angels. The differentia 'rational' (natiq), which constitutes man, cannot be predicated of angels.
This shows that definitions are level-specific.
4
Apply the principle
Understand that differentiae and definitions are restricted to their own level in the hierarchy; extrapolating them leads to logical errors.

The Hierarchy of Universals: Genera, Species, and Individuals
Author explains the hierarchy of universals from high genera to individuals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between high genera, intermediate genera, species, varieties, and individuals in the hierarchy of universals, and explain their logical relationships.

Core Idea
Universals form a hierarchy: high genera are true species when stripped of differentiae, and species divide into varieties that subsume individuals.

In this passage, the author maps the relationships among the highest genera, intermediate genera, species, varieties, and individuals. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correct definition and classification in Islamic logic. We will walk through the key distinctions and how they relate to each other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the levels of the hierarchy
Locate the terms 'high genera' (الأجناس العالية), 'species' (النوع), 'varieties' (الأصناف), and 'individuals' (الأشخاص) in the Arabic. Note how the author orders them from most universal to most particular.
The highest genera like 'substance' (الجوهر) are completely distinct from all species.
2
Distinguish high genera from intermediate genera
The author says high genera stripped of differentiae are 'true species' (أنواع حقيقية), while intermediate genera are both true and relative species. Understand that 'true species' means they can be considered species when their differentiae are removed.
This distinction is crucial for understanding how genera and species are relative terms.
3
Analyze the division of species into varieties
The species 'man' divides into varieties like 'Sindhi' and 'Hindi'. Varieties are universal subjects under the species, meaning they are still universals but more specific.
Varieties are not individuals; they are subcategories under a species.
4
Understand individuals as particulars under varieties
Individuals (e.g., Zayd, 'Amr) are particular subjects under a variety. The author emphasizes that 'man' as a species is not a concrete person; personhood requires a pointing that specifies unique characteristics.
Proper names serve as pointers, not definitions.
5
Grasp personality as a universal state
Personality (الشخصية) is a meaning that applies to all persons and attaches to the generic and specific natures. The specificity of 'this man' is more specific than 'man', just as 'man' is more specific than 'animal'.
This illustrates the logical relationship between levels: each lower level adds specificity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع ؛ وحينئذ لا يمكن تقدمها على النوع فلا يمكن أن تكون سببًا لوجوده. فتلك الحيوانية إذن بعينها هى الإنسانية والإيجاد منهما في الوجود من اللوازم على ما عرف من قبل. وأما طبائع الأجناس العالية، فإنها إذا أخذت مجردة عن فصولها صدق عليها أنها أنواع حقيقية بخلاف المتوسطات، وإنها إذا أخذت مجردة عن فصولها صدق عليها أنها حقيقية وإضافية كذلك. ولا خفاء في أن العالي من الأجناس نحو الجوهر مثلا والمفرد منها نحو العقل فإنهما مما يباين جميع مراتب النوع، والسافل من الأنواع والمفرد منها يباين جميع مراتب الجنس. ثم السافل من الأنواع ينقسم إلى الأصناف، كما أن الإنسان ينقسم إلى سندي وهندي مثلا، فالأصناف موضوعات كلية تحت النوع، والأشخاص موضوعات جزئية تحت الصنف . والنوع مثل زيد وعمرو ونحو ذلك فإنه يقال على كل واحد واحد ما يقال على الصنف والنوع فيقال إنه عربي أو عجمي؛ ويقال إنه إنسان كذلك. فالإنسان من حيث هو الإنسان لا يكون شخصا معينا؛ بل الشخص منه هو الذي يمكن أن يشار إليه إشارة يعينه ويختصه بخصائص لا يمكن وجودها بدون تلك الإشارة كما علمته في زيد وعمرو مثلا. وقد مرَّ من قبل أن الأسماء الأعلام لا تفيد فائدة في المسمى وهو الذي وضع هذا اللفظ بإزائه في الوضع الأول مثلا؛ بل هي قائمة مقام الإشارات. فالشخصية معنى يعم الأشخاص كلها، وإنها من الأحوال التي تعرض للطبائع الموضوعة للجنسية والنوعية. فكما أن هذا النوع وهو الإنسان حيوان ناطق، فالشخصي منه وهو هذا الإنسان حيوان ناطق أيضًا. والخصوصية اللازمة للشخصية في قولنا هذا الإنسان أخص من الإنسان غير الخصوصية اللازمة في قولنا الإنسان أخص من الحيوان.
The species; at that time it is not possible for them to precede the species, so they cannot be a cause for its existence. Thus the animality itself is humanity, and the bringing into existence from them in existence is among the necessary concomitants as was known before. As for the natures of the high genera, when they are taken stripped of their differentiae, it is true of them that they are true species, unlike the intermediate ones. And when they are taken stripped of their differentiae, it is true of them that they are true and relative likewise. There is no obscurity that the highest of genera, like substance for example, and the individual among them, like intellect, both are completely distinct from all ranks of the species; and the lowest of species and the individual among them are completely distinct from all ranks of the genus. Then the lowest of species divides into varieties, just as man divides into, for example, Sindhi and Hindi. So the varieties are universal subjects under the species, and the individuals are particular subjects under the variety. And the species, such as Zayd and 'Amr and the like, is predicated of each one individually just as the variety and species are predicated, so it is said he is Arab or non-Arab, and it is said he is human likewise. So man inasmuch as he is man is not a particular person; rather the person is that which can be pointed to with a pointing that specifies him and distinguishes him with characteristics that cannot exist without that pointing, as you learned in Zayd and 'Amr for example. And it has passed before that proper names do not benefit any benefit in the named, which is that for which this word was placed in the first placement for example; rather they stand in place of pointings. So personality is a meaning that encompasses all persons, and it is among the states that occur to the natures that are subject to genericness and specificness. Just as this species, which is man, is a rational animal, so the individual of it, which is this man, is also a rational animal. And the specificity necessary for personality in our saying 'this man' is more specific than man, not the specificity necessary in our saying 'man' is more specific than animal.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage discusses the hierarchy of universals, focusing on the relationships between high genera, intermediate genera, species, varieties, and individuals. The author begins by emphasizing that animality and humanity are essentially the same in reality, and their existential effect is a necessary consequence. He then explains that high genera (like substance or intellect), when taken without their differentiae, are considered true species, whereas intermediate genera can be seen as both true and relative species. The highest genera are completely distinct from all species, and the lowest species are distinct from all genera. The lowest species further divides into varieties (like Sindhi and Hindi for man), which are universal subjects under the species, while individuals are particular subjects under the variety. The author clarifies that 'man' as a species is not a particular person; personhood involves a pointing that specifies unique characteristics. Proper names do not convey meaning but serve as pointers. Personality is a universal state that applies to all persons, and it attaches to the generic and specific natures. Finally, the author notes that the special characteristic of personhood (e.g., 'this man') is more specific than the species 'man', just as 'man' is more specific than 'animal'.

Checkpoint

A) Varieties are particular subjects under individuals.

C) Varieties and individuals are both universals.
D) Individuals are universal subjects under varieties.

Key Takeaway
The hierarchy of universals moves from high genera through intermediate genera, species, varieties, to individuals, with each level adding specificity and being predicated of the lower levels.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Differentia (Fasl): Two Meanings and Their Logical Divisions
Author defines differentia and its two meanings: general and specific.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the general and specific meanings of differentia (fasl) and classify examples as general, specific-always, or specific-not-always.

Core Idea
Fasl has a broad sense (any distinction) and a narrow sense (essential distinction), further divided into reversible and irreversible types.

In the previous lesson on genus and species, you learned how categories are arranged. Now we turn to differentia (fasl), the third universal that defines what makes a thing what it is. However, logicians use 'fasl' in two distinct ways: one very broad, covering any distinguishing feature; another narrow, referring to essential distinctions. Understanding this division is crucial for constructing precise definitions (hadd) in Islamic sciences like Usul al-Fiqh and Kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two technical meanings of fasl
The passage states that fasl has two meanings for logicians: (1) 'that by which a thing is distinguished from any thing whatsoever' (general), and (2) 'that by which a thing is distinguished in its essence' (specific/transferred). Locate these definitions in the Arabic text.
2
Contrast with genus and species usage
Unlike genus and species, where the first meaning is common usage and the second is technical, here the first meaning is already technical. This shows that logicians have special terminology for differentia.
3
Examine the three divisions of differentia by priority
The author says logicians could make differentia predicated of three things according to priority: general, specific that is always a differentia, and specific that is not always. Read the examples: Zayd sitting (general), man's smooth skin (specific always), blackness for a Black person (specific not always).
The 'three things' correspond to: (a) general differentia, (b) specific differentia that never separates, and (c) specific differentia that can separate from the subject.
4
Distinguish between general and specific differentia
General differentia is reversible (Zayd can be sitting while Amr is not, and vice versa). Specific differentia is irreversible (man is smooth-skinned, horse never is). This reversibility is the key logical difference.
5
Recognize the nuance within specific differentia
Within specific differentia, some are always a differentia (like smooth skin between man and horse) and some are not always (like blackness between a black person and others, because others can become black). The distinction depends on whether the attribute can be absent from the other species/individual.
The passage suggests that specific differentia may be suitable for distinguishing individuals within one species (e.g., blackness distinguishes one human from another).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما «الفصل» فلفظة تدل على معنيين أيضًا، لكن لا يكون سبيلهما سبيل مثلهما في الجنس والنوع؛ إذ الوضع الأول في الجنس إنما هو الجمهور، والثاني وهو النقل للخواص. وههنا ليس كذلك ؛ بل المنطقيون يستعملونه على وضع أول وعلى نقل أما في الأول فإنه عبارة عما يتميز به الشيء عن شيء أي شيء كان، وفي الثاني وهو النقل عبارة عما يتميز به الشيء في ذاته. وإذا فعلوا هذا فقد كان لهم أن يجعلوا الفصل مقولا على أشياء ثلاثة بحسب التقدم والتأخر، حتى يكون من الفصل ما هو عام وهو الذي يجوز أن ينفصل به شيء عن غيره، ويجوز أن ينفصل به الشيء عن نفسه بحسب وقتين. فإن زيدًا ينفصل عن عمر و بأنه قاعد مثلا دون عمرو، ثم عمر و ينفصل عنه بأنه قاعد دون زيد، فيكون هذا الانفصال بالقوة مشتركًا بينهما. وكذلك زيد ينفصل عن نفسه في وقتين بأن يكون مرة قاعدًا ومرة ليس بقاعد ومنه ما هو خاص وهو المحمول اللازم من العرضيات، فإنه إذا وقع الانفصال بعرض غير مفارق فذلك لا يزال انفصالا خاصًا مثل انفصال الإنسان عن الفرس بكونه بادي البشرة، فإنه ينفصل به عن الفرس ولا ينفصل به الفرس عنه جاز أن يعرض للفرس هذا أو لم يجز. فمنه ما لا يزال فاصلا كما ضربتك من المثال، ومنه ما لا يكون كذلك مثل السواد الذي ينفصل به الزنجي عن غيره. فإن الزنجي لا يفارقه السواد لكن الغير من الإنسان يمكن أن يسود، فحينئذ لا يكون بينهما انفصال بالسواد؛ فحيث كان السواد فصلا كان خاصا بالزنجي. وأما العام كما مر فلا يمكن أن يكون كذلك ؛ بل تارة ينفصل هذا عن ذلك و[تارة] أخرى ذلك عن هذا، وهذا القسم من الخاص قد يصلح به أشخاص نوع واحد. وأما
As for 'differentia', it is a word indicating two meanings as well, but their way is not like that of genus and species; because the first placement in genus is for the common people, and the second is the transference for the specialists. But here it is not so; rather the logicians use it in a first placement and a transference. As for the first, it is an expression for that by which a thing is distinguished from any thing whatsoever. And the second, which is the transference, is an expression for that by which a thing is distinguished in its essence. When they did this, they could make differentia predicated of three things according to priority and posteriority, such that among differentia there is the general, which is that by which a thing may be distinguished from another, and by which a thing may be distinguished from itself with respect to two times. For Zayd is distinguished from 'Amr by his being sitting, for example, unlike 'Amr, then 'Amr is distinguished from him by his being sitting, unlike Zayd, so this distinction is potentially shared between them. Likewise, Zayd is distinguished from himself in two times by being sometimes sitting and sometimes not sitting. And among it there is the specific, which is the necessary attribute of the accidents; when the distinction occurs by a non-separable accident, that is always a specific distinction, like the distinction of man from horse by being smooth-skinned. For he is distinguished from the horse by it, and the horse is not distinguished from him by it, whether it is possible for the horse to have this or not. So among it there is that which is always a differentia, as I gave you the example, and among it there is that which is not like that, such as blackness by which the Black person is distinguished from others. For blackness does not separate from the Black person, but another person can become black; then there is no distinction between them by blackness. So when blackness was a differentia, it was specific to the Black person. As for the general, as mentioned, it cannot be like that; rather sometimes this is distinguished from that and [sometimes] that from this. And this part of the specific may be suitable for individuals of one species. And
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'differentia' (فصل) as used by logicians. The author begins by noting that 'فصل' has two meanings, but unlike genus and species, its first meaning is not common usage but a technical one. The first meaning is what distinguishes a thing from anything else; this is a broad sense. The second meaning, which is a transference, is what distinguishes a thing in its essence. Logicians then divide differentia into three types based on priority and posteriority: (1) general differentia, which can distinguish one thing from another and even a thing from itself at different times, like Zayd being sitting while 'Amr is not, or Zayd sitting at one time and not at another; (2) specific differentia, which is a necessary accident that always distinguishes, like man's smooth skin distinguishing him from a horse (the horse cannot have smooth skin); within specific, there is what is always a differentia (like smooth skin) and what is not always (like blackness for a Black person, because others can become black). The author then contrasts the general type, which is reversible, with the specific type, which is not. The passage ends while discussing that the specific differentia may be suitable for individuals of one species.

عام
خاص

B) Sitting distinguishing Zayd from 'Amr at a given moment

D) Blackness distinguishing a Black person from others

Key Takeaway
Fasl (differentia) has two technical meanings: a general sense (any distinguishing feature) and a specific sense (essential distinction), with the specific further divided into always and not always, depending on reversibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Identify which part of this definition functions as a differentia and whether it is general or specific. How would you refine it to be a proper hadd?

The Two Meanings of al-Fasl and Its Three Types
Author defines al-fasl and its two meanings, then classifies three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the general and technical meanings of al-fasl and classify any given differentia as general, specific (accidental), or specific of the specific (constitutive).

Core Idea
The differentia has a broad sense (any distinction) and a narrow logical sense (essential distinction); only the latter defines a species.

This passage dives into the concept of 'fasl' (differentia) as one of the five universals. The author carefully separates two meanings: one used by the general public for any distinguishing feature, and a technical logical meaning referring to essence-based distinction. He then classifies differentiae into three types by priority and posteriority: general, specific, and specific of the specific. Mastering this classification is essential for evaluating definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two meanings
Find where the author says 'first usage' and 'second usage' for 'fasl'. The first is general (any distinction), the second is technical (essential distinction).
The general meaning is like 'sitting' distinguishing Zayd from Amr.
2
Identify the three types
The author lists three types based on priority (general, specific, specific of specific). Find the descriptions for each.
General can distinguish both ways; specific is one-way via necessary accident; specific of specific constitutes the species.
3
Apply to examples
Classify the examples given: sitting (general), bare-skinnedness (specific), rationality (specific of specific).
Bare-skinnedness is a necessary accident for humans vs. horses; rationality is essential.
4
Test with a new Islamic example
Consider 'being a predator' for a lion. Is it a general differentia (shared with tigers) or specific?
It is likely specific accidental if it's a necessary property but not defining the essence.
5
Distinguish accidental from constitutive
The specific differentia can be accidental (like blackness) and may not always hold. The constitutive differentia always holds and defines the species.
Blackness distinguishes a Zanjī but can fail; rationality always distinguishes humans.

بأنه قاعد دون زيد، فيكون هذا الانفصال بالقوة مشتركًا بينهما. وكذلك زيد ينفصل عن نفسه في وقتين بأن يكون مرة قاعدًا ومرة ليس بقاعد. ومنه ما هو خاص وهو المحمول اللازم من العرضيات، فإنه إذا وقع الانفصال بعرض غير مفارق فذلك لا يزال انفصالًا خاصًا مثل انفصال الإنسان عن الفرس بكونه بادي البشرة، فإنه ينفصل به عن الفرس ولا ينفصل به الفرس عنه، جاز أن يعرض للفرس هذا أو لم يجز. فمنه ما لا يزال فاصلا كما ضربت كان خاصًا بالزنجي. وأما العام كما مر فلا يمكن أن يكون كذلك ؛ بل تارة ينفصل هذا عن ذلك وتارة أخرى ذلك عن هذا، وهذا القسم من الخاص قد يصلح به أشخاص نوع واحد. وأما الأول من قسمي الخاص فإنه لا ينفصل به أشخاص نوع واحد. اللهم إلا أن يكون من جملة ما يعرض من ابتداء الوجود، كما للناس في ابتداء الولادة، ولا يمكن أن يعرض بعد ذلك، فإنه مما يقع به الفصل بين أشخاص النوع. ومنه ما هو خاص للخاص وهو الفصل المقوم للنوع، وهذا هو المقصود في هذا الموضع؛ إذ هو واحد من الكليات الخمس، وهو الذي إذا قرن بطبيعة الجنس قومه نوعًا. وبعد ذلك يلزمه ما يلزمه ويعرض له ما يعرض له فهو ذاتي لطبيعة الجنس المقوم نوعًا لا لطبيعة الجنس المطلقة؛ إذ الحيوانية المطلقة مثلًا، قد تخلو عن النطق. وهذا الفصل ينفصل من سائر الأمور التي معه بأنه هو الذي يلقي أولًا طبيعة الجنس فيجعله ويصوره، وتلك الأمور يلحقها بعد ما لقيها هذا الفصل وأقرنها فاستعد للزوم ما يلزمه ولحوق ما يلحقه كالنطق. فإن القوة الناطقة التي تسمى نفسًا ناطقة لما أقرنت بالمادة فصار مثلًا الحيوان ناطقًا ليستعد لقبول العلم والكتابة والتعجب والضحك وغير ذلك. وأنت تعلم أنه لولا هذه القوة الكلية الإنسانية التي تسمى بها ناطقًا لما جعلت له هذه الاستعدادات الجزئية، وإن تلك القوة هي المسماة بالنطق فصار بها ناطقًا وهو الفصل المقوم الذاتي لطبيعة النوع. وأما أنه أسود وغيره فليس من الأشياء التي يلحق بطبيعة الجنس، فأفرد به شيئًا عرض له ولحق به، فيلزم أن يتحقق الفصل بين الفصل الذي هو خاص الخاص وبين غيره من الفصول. فلهذا يمكنك أن تقول إن من الفصول ما هو مفارق، ومنها ما هو غير مفارق، ومن ذلك الغير ما هو ذاتي ومنه ما هو عرضي. وذلك أن تقول أيضًا إن من الفصول ما تحدث غيرية، ومنها ما تحدث غيرها وهو الآخرية، والآخر هو الذي جوهره غير والغير أعم من الآخر. فكل ما يخالف شيئًا فهو غير، وليس كل ما يخالف شيئًا فهو آخر، فالفصل الذي هو خاص الخاص
As for 'al-fasl' (the differentia), it is a word that indicates two meanings as well, but their way is not like the way of those two in genus and species; because the first usage in genus is for the general public, and the second is the transfer for the specialists. But here it is not so; rather, the logicians use it in a first usage and in a transferred usage. As for the first, it is an expression for that by which a thing is distinguished from anything whatsoever. And as for the second, which is the transfer, it is an expression for that by which a thing is distinguished in its essence. And when they did this, they were able to make 'fasl' predicated of three things according to priority and posteriority, so that among 'fasl' there is the general – which is that by which a thing can be distinguished from other than it, and by which a thing can be distinguished from itself with respect to two times. For Zayd is distinguished from 'Amr by his being sitting, for example, without 'Amr, then 'Amr is distinguished from him by his being sitting without Zayd, so this distinction is potentially shared between them. And likewise Zayd is distinguished from himself in two times by being once sitting and once not sitting. And among it there is the specific – which is the necessary predicable among accidentals; for when the distinction occurs by an inseparable accident, that is always a specific distinction, like the distinction of man from horse by being bare-skinned; for he is distinguished from the horse by it, and the horse is not distinguished from him by it, whether it is possible for the horse to have this or not. So among it there is that which is always a differentia, as the example I gave you, and among it there is that which is not like that, such as blackness by which the Zanjī is distinguished from others. For blackness does not separate from the Zanjī, but the other among humans can become black; then at that time there is no distinction between them by blackness. So where blackness was a differentia, it was specific to the Zanjī. As for the general, as passed, it cannot be like that; rather, sometimes this is distinguished from that, and sometimes that is distinguished from this. And this category of the specific may differentiate the individuals of one species. As for the first of the two categories of the specific, it does not differentiate the individuals of one species, unless it is among things that occur from the beginning of existence, as for humans at the beginning of birth, and cannot occur after that, then it is that by which individuals of the species are distinguished. And among it there is that which is specific of the specific – and it is the differentia that constitutes the species. And this is the intended in this place; for it is one of the five universals, and it is that which, when coupled with the nature of the genus, constitutes a species. And after that, what is necessary for it attaches to it, and what is accidental to it occurs to it; so it is essential to the nature of the genus that constitutes a species, not to the absolute nature of the genus; for absolute animality, for example, may be devoid of rationality. And this differentia is distinguished from all other things that go with it in that it is what first throws the nature of the genus and makes it and forms it, and those other things attach after this differentia has thrown it and coupled with it, so it becomes prepared for the attachment of what is necessary and the occurrence of what is accidental, like rationality. For the rational power which is called the rational soul, when it couples with matter, then the animal becomes rational, ready to accept knowledge, writing, wonder, laughter, and other things. And you know that were it not for this universal human power by which it is called rational, these particular dispositions would not be made for it, and that power is what is called 'al-nutq' (rationality), so it becomes rational by it, and it is the constitutive essential differentia of the nature of the species. As for that it is black and other such things, it is not among the things that attach to the nature of the genus; rather, it is singled out as something accidental to it and attached to it. So it is necessary to verify the distinction between the differentia that is specific of the specific and other differentiae. For this reason you can say that among differentiae there is separable, and among them there is inseparable, and among the inseparable is essential and among it is accidental. And you can also say that among differentiae there are those that produce otherness (ghayriyya), and among them those that produce otherness of another kind which is alterity (ākharīyya). And 'al-ākhar' is that whose essence is other (ghayr), and 'al-ghayr' is more general than 'al-ākhar'. For everything that differs from something is 'ghayr', but not everything that differs from something is 'ākhar'. So the differentia that is specific of the specific...
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed definition and classification of 'al-fasl' (the differentia) as one of the five universals. The author begins by noting that 'fasl' has two meanings, unlike genus and species which also have two meanings but with a different pattern. The first meaning of 'fasl' is general: that by which any thing is distinguished from any other thing whatsoever. The second meaning, which is the technical logical usage, is that by which a thing is distinguished in its essence. Based on these, the author breaks 'fasl' into three types according to priority and posteriority. The first type is 'al-ʿāmm' (the general differentia), which can apply in both directions (e.g., Zayd is distinguished from Amr by sitting, and Amr from Zayd by sitting) and also can distinguish a thing from itself at different times (e.g., Zayd sitting vs. not sitting). The second type is 'al-khāṣṣ' (the specific differentia), which is a necessary accident that distinguishes one thing from another in a one-way manner. Examples include the distinction of man from horse by being bare-skinned (bādi al-bashara), which always holds for man and never for horse. Another example is blackness distinguishing a Zanjī from others, but this distinction can break if another human becomes black. The author distinguishes between two sub-types of this specific differentia: one that always remains a differentia (like bare-skinnedness for man vs. horse) and one that does not (like blackness for the Zanjī). The third type is 'khāṣṣ al-khāṣṣ' (the specific of the specific), which is the constitutive differentia that forms the species when joined with the genus. This is the primary concern in logic as one of the five universals. The author explains that this differentia is essential (dhātī) to the nature of the genus that constitutes a species, not to the absolute genus. For example, absolute animality can exist without rationality, but when rationality is added, it constitutes the species 'rational animal' (human). The author elaborates on how the rational power (al-nāṭiqa) prepares the animal for various accidents like knowledge, writing, etc. Finally, the author distinguishes between separable (mufāriq) and inseparable (ghayr mufāriq) differentiae, and within inseparable between essential and accidental. Additionally, the author introduces the distinction between 'ghayriyya' (otherness) and 'ākharīyya' (alterity), noting that 'ghayr' is more general than 'ākhar': everything that differs is 'ghayr', but not everything that differs is 'ākhar' (which implies a difference in essence). The passage ends mid-sentence with 'so the differentia that is specific of the specific...', likely continuing to elaborate on this concept.

خاص الخاص
غير
آخر

Key Takeaway
The differentia (fasl) has two meanings: general (any distinction) and logical (essential), and it is classified into three types: general, specific accidental, and constitutive (خاص الخاص).

The Constitutive Differentia (Khass al-Khass) and Essential vs. Accidental Distinction
Author focuses on the constitutive differentia and related distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a constitutive differentia (like rationality) is essential and how it differs from accidental differentiae, and you will be able to apply the separable/inseparable and ghayr/akhar distinctions to Islamic examples.

Core Idea
The constitutive differentia (خاص الخاص) is the essential property that defines a species; all other properties depend on it.

In this section, the author zeroes in on the most important type of differentia: the constitutive differentia (khass al-khass), which is one of the five universals. He explains how it works: it 'throws' the genus and forms the species, and then other accidents attach to it. He also distinguishes between separable and inseparable differentiae, and between essential and accidental within inseparable. Finally, he introduces the logical distinction between 'ghayr' (general otherness) and 'ākhar' (essential otherness). This lesson helps you understand the core tool for defining any species in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the constitutive differentia
Find where the author says 'خاص الخاص' and that it is the differentia that constitutes the species. Note its role: when coupled with the genus, it forms the species.
The example used is rationality (النطق) for humans.
2
Analyze the example of rationality
The author explains that rationality (the rational soul) first joins with animality, making the animal rational, and then enables other accidents like knowledge, writing, etc.
This shows that rationality is essential, while knowledge and writing are accidental.
3
Distinguish separable vs. inseparable
The author says: among differentiae there are separable (مفارق) and inseparable (غير مفارق). Find this part and note examples.
Separable like sitting, inseparable like blackness (but blackness is accidental inseparable).
4
Understand the ghayr/ākhar distinction
The author ends by distinguishing 'ghayr' (general otherness) from 'ākhar' (essential otherness). Note that every 'ākhar' is 'ghayr' but not vice versa.
This distinction helps in defining species by essence vs. accident.
5
Apply to an Islamic science example
Consider the definition of 'sunna' in fiqh: is it a constitutive differentia or an accidental one relative to the genus 'act of worship'?
This forces you to think about what makes an act 'sunna' essentially.

وضع أول وعلى نقل أما في الأول فإنه عبارة عما يتميز به الشيء عن شيء أي شيء كان، وفي الثاني وهو النقل عبارة عما يتميز به الشيء في ذاته. وإذا فعلوا هذا فقد كان لهم أن يجعلوا الفصل مقولا على أشياء ثلاثة بحسب التقدم والتأخر، حتى يكون من الفصل ما هو عام وهو الذي يجوز أن ينفصل به شيء عن غيره، ويجوز أن ينفصل به الشيء عن نفسه بحسب وقتين. فإن زيدًا ينفصل عن عمرو بأنه قاعد مثلًا دون عمرو، ثم عمرو ينفصل عنه بأنه قاعد دون زيد، فيكون هذا الانفصال بالقوة مشتركًا بينهما. وكذلك زيد ينفصل عن نفسه في وقتين بأن يكون مرة قاعدًا ومرة ليس بقاعد. ومنه ما هو خاص وهو المحمول اللازم من العرضيات، فإنه إذا وقع الانفصال بعرض غير مفارق فذلك لا يزال انفصالًا خاصًا مثل انفصال الإنسان عن الفرس بكونه بادي البشرة، فإنه ينفصل به عن الفرس ولا ينفصل به الفرس عنه، جاز أن يعرض للفرس هذا أو لم يجز. فمنه ما لا يزال فاصلا كما ضربت لك من المثال، ومنه ما لا يكون كذلك مثل السواد الذي ينفصل به الزنجي عن غيره. فإن الزنجي لا يفارقه السواد لكن الغير من الإنسان يمكن أن يسود، فحينئذ لا يكون بينهما انفصال بالسواد؛ فحيث كان السواد فصلا كان خاصًا بالزنجي. وأما العام كما مر فلا يمكن أن يكون كذلك ؛ بل تارة ينفصل هذا عن ذلك وتارة أخرى ذلك عن هذا، وهذا القسم من الخاص قد يصلح به أشخاص نوع واحد. وأما الأول من قسمي الخاص فإنه لا ينفصل به أشخاص نوع واحد. اللهم إلا أن يكون من جملة ما يعرض من ابتداء الوجود، كما للناس في ابتداء الولادة، ولا يمكن أن يعرض بعد ذلك، فإنه مما يقع به الفصل بين أشخاص النوع. ومنه ما هو خاص للخاص وهو الفصل المقوم للنوع، وهذا هو المقصود في هذا الموضع؛ إذ هو واحد من الكليات الخمس، وهو الذي إذا قرن بطبيعة الجنس قومه نوعًا. وبعد ذلك يلزمه ما يلزمه ويعرض له ما يعرض له فهو ذاتي لطبيعة الجنس المقوم نوعًا لا لطبيعة الجنس المطلقة؛ إذ الحيوانية المطلقة مثلًا، قد تخلو عن النطق. وهذا الفصل ينفصل من سائر الأمور التي معه بأنه هو الذي يلقي أولًا طبيعة الجنس فيجعله ويصوره، وتلك الأمور يلحقها بعد ما لقيها هذا الفصل وأقرنها فاستعد للزوم ما يلزمه ولحوق ما يلحقه كالنطق. فإن القوة الناطقة التي تسمى نفسًا ناطقة لما أقرنت بالمادة فصار مثلًا الحيوان ناطقًا ليستعد لقبول العلم والكتابة والتعجب والضحك وغير ذلك. وأنت تعلم أنه لولا هذه القوة الكلية الإنسانية التي تسمى بها ناطقًا لما جعلت له هذه الاستعدادات الجزئية، وإن تلك القوة هي المسماة بالنطق فصار بها ناطقًا وهو الفصل المقوم الذاتي لطبيعة النوع. وأما أنه أسود وغيره فليس من الأشياء التي يلحق بطبيعة الجنس، فأفرد به شيئًا عرض له ولحق به، فيلزم أن يتحقق الفصل بين الفصل الذي هو خاص الخاص وبين غيره من الفصول. فلهذا يمكنك أن تقول إن من الفصول ما هو مفارق، ومنها ما هو غير مفارق، ومن ذلك الغير ما هو ذاتي ومنه ما هو عرضي. وذلك أن تقول أيضًا إن من الفصول ما تحدث غيرية، ومنها ما تحدث غيرها وهو الآخرية، والآخر هو الذي جوهره غير والغير أعم من الآخر. فكل ما يخالف شيئًا فهو غير، وليس كل ما يخالف شيئًا فهو آخر، فالفصل الذي هو خاص الخاص
As for 'al-fasl' (the differentia), it is a word that indicates two meanings as well, but their way is not like the way of those two in genus and species; because the first usage in genus is for the general public, and the second is the transfer for the specialists. But here it is not so; rather, the logicians use it in a first usage and in a transferred usage. As for the first, it is an expression for that by which a thing is distinguished from anything whatsoever. And as for the second, which is the transfer, it is an expression for that by which a thing is distinguished in its essence. And when they did this, they were able to make 'fasl' predicated of three things according to priority and posteriority, so that among 'fasl' there is the general – which is that by which a thing can be distinguished from other than it, and by which a thing can be distinguished from itself with respect to two times. For Zayd is distinguished from 'Amr by his being sitting, for example, without 'Amr, then 'Amr is distinguished from him by his being sitting without Zayd, so this distinction is potentially shared between them. And likewise Zayd is distinguished from himself in two times by being once sitting and once not sitting. And among it there is the specific – which is the necessary predicable among accidentals; for when the distinction occurs by an inseparable accident, that is always a specific distinction, like the distinction of man from horse by being bare-skinned; for he is distinguished from the horse by it, and the horse is not distinguished from him by it, whether it is possible for the horse to have this or not. So among it there is that which is always a differentia, as the example I gave you, and among it there is that which is not like that, such as blackness by which the Zanjī is distinguished from others. For blackness does not separate from the Zanjī, but the other among humans can become black; then at that time there is no distinction between them by blackness. So where blackness was a differentia, it was specific to the Zanjī. As for the general, as passed, it cannot be like that; rather, sometimes this is distinguished from that, and sometimes that is distinguished from this. And this category of the specific may differentiate the individuals of one species. As for the first of the two categories of the specific, it does not differentiate the individuals of one species, unless it is among things that occur from the beginning of existence, as for humans at the beginning of birth, and cannot occur after that, then it is that by which individuals of the species are distinguished. And among it there is that which is specific of the specific – and it is the differentia that constitutes the species. And this is the intended in this place; for it is one of the five universals, and it is that which, when coupled with the nature of the genus, constitutes a species. And after that, what is necessary for it attaches to it, and what is accidental to it occurs to it; so it is essential to the nature of the genus that constitutes a species, not to the absolute nature of the genus; for absolute animality, for example, may be devoid of rationality. And this differentia is distinguished from all other things that go with it in that it is what first throws the nature of the genus and makes it and forms it, and those other things attach after this differentia has thrown it and coupled with it, so it becomes prepared for the attachment of what is necessary and the occurrence of what is accidental, like rationality. For the rational power which is called the rational soul, when it couples with matter, then the animal becomes rational, ready to accept knowledge, writing, wonder, laughter, and other things. And you know that were it not for this universal human power by which it is called rational, these particular dispositions would not be made for it, and that power is what is called 'al-nutq' (rationality), so it becomes rational by it, and it is the constitutive essential differentia of the nature of the species. As for that it is black and other such things, it is not among the things that attach to the nature of the genus; rather, it is singled out as something accidental to it and attached to it. So it is necessary to verify the distinction between the differentia that is specific of the specific and other differentiae. For this reason you can say that among differentiae there is separable, and among them there is inseparable, and among the inseparable is essential and among it is accidental. And you can also say that among differentiae there are those that produce otherness (ghayriyya), and among them those that produce otherness of another kind which is alterity (ākharīyya). And 'al-ākhar' is that whose essence is other (ghayr), and 'al-ghayr' is more general than 'al-ākhar'. For everything that differs from something is 'ghayr', but not everything that differs from something is 'ākhar'. So the differentia that is specific of the specific...
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed definition and classification of 'al-fasl' (the differentia) as one of the five universals. The author begins by noting that 'fasl' has two meanings, unlike genus and species which also have two meanings but with a different pattern. The first meaning of 'fasl' is general: that by which any thing is distinguished from any other thing whatsoever. The second meaning, which is the technical logical usage, is that by which a thing is distinguished in its essence. Based on these, the author breaks 'fasl' into three types according to priority and posteriority. The first type is 'al-ʿāmm' (the general differentia), which can apply in both directions (e.g., Zayd is distinguished from Amr by sitting, and Amr from Zayd by sitting) and also can distinguish a thing from itself at different times (e.g., Zayd sitting vs. not sitting). The second type is 'al-khāṣṣ' (the specific differentia), which is a necessary accident that distinguishes one thing from another in a one-way manner. Examples include the distinction of man from horse by being bare-skinned (bādi al-bashara), which always holds for man and never for horse. Another example is blackness distinguishing a Zanjī from others, but this distinction can break if another human becomes black. The author distinguishes between two sub-types of this specific differentia: one that always remains a differentia (like bare-skinnedness for man vs. horse) and one that does not (like blackness for the Zanjī). The third type is 'khāṣṣ al-khāṣṣ' (the specific of the specific), which is the constitutive differentia that forms the species when joined with the genus. This is the primary concern in logic as one of the five universals. The author explains that this differentia is essential (dhātī) to the nature of the genus that constitutes a species, not to the absolute genus. For example, absolute animality can exist without rationality, but when rationality is added, it constitutes the species 'rational animal' (human). The author elaborates on how the rational power (al-nāṭiqa) prepares the animal for various accidents like knowledge, writing, etc. Finally, the author distinguishes between separable (mufāriq) and inseparable (ghayr mufāriq) differentiae, and within inseparable between essential and accidental. Additionally, the author introduces the distinction between 'ghayriyya' (otherness) and 'ākharīyya' (alterity), noting that 'ghayr' is more general than 'ākhar': everything that differs is 'ghayr', but not everything that differs is 'ākhar' (which implies a difference in essence). The passage ends mid-sentence with 'so the differentia that is specific of the specific...', likely continuing to elaborate on this concept.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about the constitutive differentia (خاص الخاص)?
A) It can be separable from the species
B) It is the first to join with the genus and forms the species
C) It is an accidental property
D) It distinguishes individuals of a species from each other

Key Takeaway
The constitutive differentia (خاص الخاص) is the essential differentia that defines a species; it is separable from other differentiae, and the distinction between general otherness (ghayr) and essential otherness (akhar) helps in precise definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In a fiqh discussion, the 'illa (cause) for allowing tayammum (dry ablution) is travel or illness. Are these essential differentiae or accidental? Use the author's separable/inseparable and essential/accidental distinctions.
?
The author says that 'al-akhar' is that whose essence is other, while 'al-ghayr' is more general. Give an Islamic example where two things are different by 'ghayr' but not by 'akhar' (e.g., two types of animals with different accidents but same essence).

The Five Universals
advanced
8 min
The Specific Differentia: Definition, Properties, and Role
Author defines the specific differentia and discusses its properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the specific differentia (al-fasl al-khass bi-l-khass) and distinguish it from other differentiate using its properties (essential, not privative, not subject to intensity, and its role as essential cause).

Core Idea
The specific differentia is the essential cause of otherness that constitutes the species when joined with the genus.

The specific differentia (al-fasl al-khass bi-l-khass) is one of the five universals and the key to defining a species. In this passage, the author explains how to identify this differentia, what properties it must have, and why it cannot be a privation or subject to variation. Understanding this tool is essential for constructing accurate definitions (hadd) in Islamic sciences such as usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term defined
Locate the term 'al-fasl al-khass bi-l-khass' in the Arabic. The author explicitly says it is the fifth universal and the one that constitutes the species when coupled with the genus.
2
Extract the definition
From the passage, write down the definition: 'the universal essential said in answer to “What sort of thing is it?”' (al-kulli al-dhati al-maqul fi jawab 'ayy ma huwa'). Note what each part excludes.
'Universal essential' excludes property and general accident; 'in answer to “What sort of thing is it?”' excludes genus, species, and general accident.
3
Examine the properties
The author states the differentia cannot be susceptible to intensity/weakness (because quiddities are not variable) and cannot be a privation ('adami) because non-existence cannot constitute existent things. Also, it is a cause of the specific characteristic according to the stronger view.
4
Understand the causal role
The differentia is the essential cause (illa dhatiyya) of the difference that necessitates otherness (ukhra). It is what first acts on the genus, giving it form and preparing it for subsequent properties.
5
Classify differentiate
The author classifies differentiate: some are separable, some inseparable; among inseparable, some are essential, some accidental. Also, some produce 'different' (ghayr) and some produce 'other' (akhar). The specific differentia produces otherness.

الأول من قسمى الخاص فإنه لا ينفصل به أشخاص نوع واحد. اللهم إلا أن يكون من جملة ما يعرض من ابتداء الوجود، كما للناس في ابتداء الولادة، ولا يمكن أن يعرض بعد ذلك، فإنه مما يقع به الفصل بين أشخاص النوع. ومنه ما هو خاص للخاص وهو الفصل المقوم للنوع، وهذا هو المقصود في هذا الموضع؛ إذ هو واحد من الكليات الخمس، وهو الذي إذا قرن بطبيعة الجنس قومه نوعًا. وبعد ذلك يلزمه ما يلزمه ويعرض له ما يعرض له فهو ذاتي لطبيعة الجنس المقوم نوعًا لا لطبيعة الجنس المطلقة؛ إذ الحيوانية المطلقة مثلًا، قد يخلو عن النطق. وهذا الفصل ينفصل من سائر الأمور التي معه بأنه هو الذي يلقي أولا طبيعة الجنس فيجعله ويصوره، وتلك الأمور يلحقها بعد ما لقيها هذا الفصل وأقرنها فاستعد للزوم ما يلزمه ولحوق ما يلحقه كالنطق. فإن القوة الناطقة التي تسمى نفسًا ناطقة لما أقرنت بالمادة فصار مثلا الحيوان ناطقا ليستعد لقبول العلم والكتابة والتعجب والضحك وغير ذلك. وأنت تعلم أنه لولا هذه القوة الكلية الإنسانية التي تسمى بها ناطقا لما جعلت له هذه الاستعدادات الجزئية، وإن تلك القوة هي المسماة بالنطق فصار بها ناطقا وهو الفصل المقوم الذاتي لطبيعة النوع. وأما أنه أسود وغيره فليس من الأشياء التي يلحق بطبيعة الجنس، فأفرد به شيئًا عرض له ولحق به، فيلزم أن يتحقق الفصل بين الفصل الذي هو خاص الخاص وبين غيره من الفصول. فلهذا يمكنك أن تقول إن من الفصول ما هو مفارق، ومنها ما هو غير مفارق، ومن ذلك الغير ما هو ذاتي ومنه ما هو عرضي. وذلك أن تقول أيضًا إن من الفصول ما تحدث غيرية، ومنها ما تحدث غيرها وهو الآخرية، والآخر هو الذي جوهره غير والغير أعم من الآخر. فكل ما يخالف شيئًا فهو غير، وليس كل ما يخالف شيئًا فهو آخر، فالفصل الذي هو خاص الخاص هو العلة الذاتية للخلاف الموجب للآخرية بحسب اصطلاح أهل الصناعة [المنطقية] في استعمال لفظ الآخر. والمشهور في تعريف هذا الفصل أنه الكلي الذاتي المقول في جواب «أي ما هو؟»، فقولنا الكلي الذاتي يخرج الخاصة والعَرَض العام، وقولنا في جواب أي ما هو يخرج الجنس والنوع والعرض العام أيضًا. ثم إنه بالنسبة إلى الطبيعة الجنسية مقسم لها وبالنسبة إلى خصة النوع من الجنس مقوم لها، وبالنسبة إلى النوع جزء له، والجزء المقوم لا محالة ولا يمكن أن يكون قابلا للشدة والضعف، وإلا لكانت الماهية قابلة، وذلك محال فإن ماهية الشيء وذاته لا تكون قابلة للشدة والضعف ولا للزيادة والنقصان كذلك؛ إذ الأشد غير الأضعف، والأزيد غير الأنقص . فإن كانت الماهية هي الأنقص فالأزيد غير الماهية ، وإن كانت هي الأزيد فالأنقص غيرها كذلك، ولا يمكن أن يكون عدميّا أيضًا؛ فإن من المحال أن يكون العدم من حيث هو العدم من المعاني المقومة للأشياء الموجودة في الأعيان. فأما في الاعتبارية فإنه يمكن كما مر ولا يمكن أن يكون هذا الجزء على الفصل علة لخصة النوع من الجنس عند البعض؛ بل يجب أن يكون علة، فإن الجنس لا يمكن أن يكون نوعا معينا ولا خصة لذلك النوع إلا بوجود الفصل فيكون قوامها به، وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون علة. وعند بعضهم لا يجب أن يكون علة لخصة النوع من الجنس لما أن الفصل قد يكون صفة كما مرّ من قبل، والصفة مما يفتقر في الوجود إلى الموصوف، والمفتقر إلى الشيء لا يمكن أن يكون علة لذلك الشيء لكنه ضعيف جدًّا. فإنه إذا كان علة لكان علة لما يفتقر إليه في الوجود وهو الخصة، ولما كان الفصل مقسما للجنس ومقوما للنوع؛ والجنس للشيء قد يكون نوعًا لغيره، والنوع للشيء قد يكون جنسًا لغيره كذلك، فلا يمتنع أن
The first of the two divisions of the specific (al-khass) is that by which the individuals of a single species are not distinguished, unless it is among what occurs from the beginning of existence, as with people at the beginning of birth, and it cannot occur afterwards; for it is what distinguishes between individuals of the species. Among them is what is specific to the specific (al-khass bi-l-khass), which is the constitutive differentia (al-fasl al-muqawwim) of the species, and this is the intended [meaning] in this place; since it is one of the five universals, and it is that which when coupled with the nature of the genus constitutes the species. After that, what necessarily follows it follows it, and what occurs to it occurs to it; so it is essential (dhati) to the nature of the genus insofar as it constitutes a species, not to the absolute nature of the genus; for absolute animality, for example, may be devoid of rationality. And this differentia is distinguished from the other matters that accompany it by the fact that it is what first strikes the nature of the genus, making it and forming it; those other matters attach after this differentia has struck and coupled with it, so it becomes prepared for the necessary following and attachment of what attaches to it, like rationality. For the rational power, which is called the rational soul, when it couples with matter and thus, for example, the animal becomes rational, it becomes prepared to receive knowledge, writing, wonder, laughter, and so on. And you know that were it not for this universal human power, by which it is called rational, these particular dispositions would not have been made for it; and that power is called 'rationality' (nutq), by which it becomes rational, and it is the essential constitutive differentia of the nature of the species. As for its being black or other [accidents], these are not among the things that attach to the nature of the genus; rather, something that occurs to it and attaches to it is singled out by it. Hence it follows that the distinction between the differentia that is specific to the specific and other differentiate is realized. For this reason, you can say that among the differentiate are separable (mufariq) and inseparable (ghayr mufariq); among the inseparable are essential (dhati) and accidental (aradi). And you can also say that among the differentiate are those that produce unlikeness (ghayriyya), and among them are those that produce otherness (ukhra), and the 'other' (al-akhar) is that whose essence is different (ghayr), while the 'different' (al-ghayr) is more general than the 'other'. For everything that differs from something is different (ghayr), but not everything that differs from something is other (akhar). So the differentia that is specific to the specific is the essential cause of the difference that necessitates otherness, according to the terminology of the people of the [logical] art in their usage of the word 'other'. The well-known definition of this differentia is that it is the universal essential (al-kulli al-dhati) said in answer to 'What sort of thing is it? (ayy ma huwa)'. So our saying 'the universal essential' excludes the property (al-khassa) and the general accident (al-arad al-amm); and our saying 'in answer to 'What sort of thing is it?' excludes the genus, the species, and also the general accident. Then, in relation to the generic nature, it is a divider of it; in relation to the specific characteristic (khassa) of the species from the genus, it is constitutive of it; and in relation to the species, it is a part of it. And the constitutive part is necessarily [such], and it cannot be susceptible to intensity and weakness; otherwise, the quiddity (mahiyya) would be susceptible, which is impossible, for the quiddity and essence of a thing are not susceptible to intensity and weakness nor to increase and decrease, likewise; for the more intense is different from the less intense, and the greater is different from the lesser. If the quiddity were the lesser, then the greater would be other than the quiddity; and if it were the greater, then the lesser would be other than it, likewise. Nor can it be privative ('adami); for it is impossible that non-existence, qua non-existence, be among the constitutive meanings of things existing in the external world. As for conceptual [meanings], it is possible, as has passed. And this part – the differentia – cannot be a cause of the specific characteristic of the species from the genus according to some; rather, it must be a cause, for the genus cannot be a specific species nor have a specific characteristic except by the existence of the differentia, so its subsistence is by it, and then it follows that it is a cause. According to some, it need not be a cause of the specific characteristic of the species from the genus, because the differentia may be an attribute (sifa), as has passed, and the attribute is, in existence, dependent on the described (al-mawsuf); and that which is dependent on a thing cannot be a cause of that thing. But this is very weak. For if it were a cause, it would be a cause of that which is dependent on it in existence, namely the specific characteristic; and since the differentia is a divider of the genus and a constitutive [part] of the species; and the genus of a thing may be a species for another, and the species of a thing may be a genus for another, likewise, it is not impossible that...
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the specific differentia (al-fasl al-khass bi-l-khass), which is the fifth universal in the traditional scheme. The author begins by distinguishing two types of 'specific' (khass): one that distinguishes individuals within a species (like accidental features at birth) and the one that is truly specific to the specific—the constitutive differentia that forms the species. This latter is the focus. The author explains that when this differentia joins with the genus, it constitutes the species. It is essential (dhati) to the genus as constituted, not to the absolute genus. For example, 'rationality' is essential to 'human' but not to 'animal' absolutely, since animality can exist without rationality. The differentia is what first acts upon the genus, giving it form; other properties then follow. The rational power (nutq) is used as the example: when it couples with the animal body, it makes the human prepared for knowledge, laughter, etc. Without this universal power, these particular dispositions would not exist. The author then distinguishes this differentia from accidental features like blackness, which are not essential to the genus. Differentiae are classified into separable and inseparable, and within inseparable, into essential and accidental. A further distinction is made between 'different' (ghayr) and 'other' (akhar): everything that is other is different, but not vice versa. The specific differentia is the essential cause of the difference that necessitates otherness. The standard definition is then given: the universal essential said in answer to 'What sort of thing is it?'. This excludes property (khassa) and general accident (arad amm) by 'universal essential', and excludes genus, species, and general accident by 'in answer to 'What sort of thing is it?'. In relation to the genus, the differentia divides it; in relation to the specific characteristic, it constitutes it; in relation to the species, it is a part. The author argues that the differentia cannot be subject to intensity or weakness because that would imply the quiddity is variable, which is impossible. It also cannot be a privation (adami), since non-existence cannot constitute existing things conceptually, though it can in mental considerations. Finally, a debate is presented: some say the differentia must be a cause of the specific characteristic because the genus cannot have a specific nature without it; others say it need not be a cause because the differentia may be an attribute dependent on the subject, and what is dependent cannot cause that upon which it depends. The author dismisses this latter view as very weak, arguing that if the differentia were a cause, it would cause what depends on it (the specific characteristic), and since it is a divider and constituent, it is not impossible for it to be a cause.

Key Terms
الفصل الخاص بالخاص
خاص
علة ذاتية
آخر
عدم

Checkpoint

A) Because privation is impossible in any conceptual framework.
B) Because non-existence cannot be a constitutive meaning of things that exist in the external world.
C) Because the differentia must be an attribute of the genus.
D) Because the differentia is always accidental.

Key Takeaway
The specific differentia is the universal essential said in answer to 'What sort of thing is it?', and it must be essential, not privative, and not subject to intensity; it is the essential cause of otherness that constitutes the species.

Defining the Differentia: What it is and What it Excludes
Author defines differentia and states it is a constitutive part not subject to intensity or non-being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the differentia in a given definition and verify it meets the criteria of being a universal essential predicate in answer to 'what is it?'.

Core Idea
The differentia is the essential distinguisher that must answer 'what is it?', not an accident or property.

In this lesson, we unpack the well-known definition of differentia (al-fasl). The author provides a precise formulation that excludes other universals. We will learn how to apply this definition to distinguish the differentia from genus, species, property, and general accident.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the definiens
What is being defined? (the differentia). What is the definition given? ('the universal essential predicate in answer to what is it?')
2
Parse the components of the definition
Break down 'universal essential' and 'in answer to what is it' and understand what each part excludes.
'Universal essential' excludes property (al-khassa) and general accident (al-‘arad al-‘amm). 'In answer to what is it' excludes genus, species, and also general accident.
3
Apply the exclusion test
For each universal (species, genus, property, accident), check if it is excluded by the definition and why.
4
Practice with an Islamic example
Take a definition from fiqh or kalam and identify whether it includes a proper differentia.
Example: 'الصلاة هي أقوال وأفعال مفتتحة بالتكبير مختتمة بالتسليم' (Prayer is sayings and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim). The genus is 'sayings and actions', the differentia is 'beginning with takbir and ending with taslim'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو العلة الذاتية للخلاف الموجب للآخرية بحسب اصطلاح أهل الصناعة المنطقية في استعمال لفظ الآخر. والمشهور في تعريف هذا الفصل أنه الكلي الذاتي المقول في جواب «أي ما هو؟»، فقولنا الكلي الذاتي يخرج الخاصة والعَرَض العام، وقولنا في جواب أي ما هو يخرج الجنس والنوع والعرض العام أيضًا. ثم إنه بالنسبة إلى الطبيعة الجنسية مقسم لها وبالنسبة إلى خصة النوع من الجنس مقوم لها، وبالنسبة إلى النوع جزء له، والجزء المقوم لا محالة ولا يمكن أن يكون قابلا للشدة والضعف، وإلا لكانت الماهية قابلة، وذلك محال فإن ماهية الشيء وذاته لا تكون قابلة للشدة والضعف ولا للزيادة والنقصان كذلك؛ إذ الأشد غير الأضعف، والأزيد غير الأنقص . فإن كانت الماهية هي الأنقص فالأزيد غير الماهية ، وإن كانت هي الأزيد فالأنقص غيرها كذلك، ولا يمكن أن يكون عدميّا أيضًا؛ فإن من المحال أن يكون العدم من حيث هو العدم من المعاني المقومة للأشياء الموجودة في الأعيان. فأما في الاعتبارية فإنه يمكن كما مر
It is the essential cause of the difference that necessitates otherness according to the terminology of the people of the logical craft in their use of the word 'other'. And the well-known definition of this differentia is that it is the universal essential predicate in answer to 'what is it?'. So our saying 'universal essential' excludes the property and the general accident, and our saying 'in answer to what is it?' excludes the genus, species, and also the general accident. Then, in relation to the generic nature it is a divisor of it, and in relation to the specificity of the species from the genus it is a constituent of it, and in relation to the species it is a part for it. The constitutive part necessarily cannot be subject to intensity and weakness, otherwise the essence would be subject, and that is impossible. For the quiddity of a thing and its essence are not subject to intensity and weakness, nor to increase and decrease likewise. Since the more intense is other than the less intense, and the more is other than the less. So if the essence is the less, then the more is other than the essence, and if it is the more, then the less is other than it likewise. And it also cannot be non-existential, for it is impossible that non-existence as non-existence should be among the constitutive meanings of things existing in external entities. As for in theoretical [matters], it is possible, as has passed.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage defines the logical differentia (al-fasl) and outlines its essential properties. The author begins by giving a definition familiar to the practitioners of logic: the differentia is the essential cause of the difference that necessitates otherness. Then he presents the more common definition: it is the universal essential predicate that is given in answer to the question 'what is it?'. This definition is explained by showing what it excludes. The phrase 'universal essential' excludes the property (al-khassa) and the general accident (al-‘arad al-‘amm) because these are not essential. The phrase 'in answer to what is it?' excludes the genus, the species, and also the general accident (though general accident is already excluded by the first part). The differentia plays multiple roles: it divides the genus (i.e., splits it into species), it constitutes the specificity (khassa) of the species within the genus, and it is a part (juz’) of the species. As a constitutive part, it cannot accept intensity or weakness; otherwise, the essence (mahiyya) itself would be subject to variation, which is impossible because the essence of a thing is fixed. He gives an argument: if the essence were the weaker, then the stronger would be other than the essence, and vice versa. Furthermore, the differentia cannot be a privation (adam), because nonexistence cannot be a constitutive principle for actual existents. However, in mental or relational matters (i‘tibariyya), it may be possible. All examples must be from Islamic sciences: e.g., the differentia 'rational' (natiq) constitutes the species 'human' and divides the genus 'animal'.

Why the Differentia Cannot Admit Intensity or Non-Being
Author defines differentia and states it is a constitutive part not subject to intensity or non-being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the argument that the differentia must be free from intensity and non-existence and apply it to essential definitions in Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
If the differentia allowed intensity, the essence itself would vary—impossible for fixed essences.

The passage argues that the differentia, as a constitutive part, cannot vary in intensity or be a non-existential. This is not just a logical curiosity—it has implications for defining real essences in metaphysics and usul al-fiqh. We will analyze this argument and see why essential definitions must be stable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
The differentia cannot accept intensity or weakness, nor can it be non-existential.
2
Extract the argument for intensity
The author gives a reductio: if the differentia admitted intensity, then the essence (mahiyya) would be subject to intensity, but essence is fixed (the more intense is other than the less).
This is a modus tollens argument: If differentia admits intensity, then essence varies. But essence does not vary. Therefore differentia does not admit intensity.
3
Extract the argument for non-existence
Non-existence cannot be a constitutive part of an existing thing because non-existence as such has no positive reality.
The author allows that in mental or relational matters, non-being might be constitutive, but not for real existents.
4
Apply to an Islamic science example
Consider the definition of 'angel' as 'jism nurani, natiq' (luminous, rational body). Could 'rational' admit intensity? No, because rationality is either present or absent; essential attributes are binary.
